# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've successfully analyzed the three repositories and created a comprehensive answer file. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

### **Kubernetes/Kubernetes**
- **Signal Handler**: `SetupSignalContext()` in `signal.go` with platform-specific definitions (POSIX registers SIGTERM+SIGINT, Windows registers only SIGINT)
- **Shutdown Timeout**: 60 seconds (configurable via `ShutdownTimeout`)
- **Cleanup Chain**: Uses sophisticated `lifecycleSignals` to orchestrate: ShutdownInitiated → AfterShutdownDelayDuration → HTTPServerStoppedListening → InFlightRequestsDrained → PreShutdownHooksStopped

### **Grafana/Grafana**
- **Signal Handler**: `listenToSystemSignals()` in `cli.go` registers for SIGTERM and SIGINT
- **Shutdown Timeout**: 30 seconds context timeout; gRPC uses 10-second default
- **Cleanup Ordering**: Simple timeout-based approach - create timeout context, call `Shutdown()`, force stop on timeout

### **Prometheus/Prometheus**
- **Signal Handler**: Uses `oklog/run.Group` pattern, registers for SIGTERM, SIGINT, and SIGHUP
- **Shutdown Timeout**: Component-specific, no global timeout in signal handler
- **Cleanup Chain**: Dependency-ordered shutdown: Discovery → RuleManager → ScrapeManager → TSDB, ensuring no writes to closed storage

The answer file has been created at `/workspace/answer.json` with detailed documentation of all files, symbols, and the execution chain for graceful shutdown across these three major Go services.

All background services and modules are shut down through the manager adapter\\n\\n### Prometheus/Prometheus\\n\\n**Signal Registration:** Prometheus implements sophisticated signal handling using the `oklog/run` package in `cmd/prometheus/main.go`. It registers for both `os.Interrupt` and `syscall.SIGTERM` (line 1155), as well as `syscall.SIGHUP` for reload signals (line 1266).\\n\\n**Shutdown Timeout:** The shutdown coordination uses the `run.Group` pattern without an explicit timeout at the signal handler level. Instead, individual components manage their own shutdown timeouts. For example, config reloaders have cancellation channels, and the scrape manager, rule manager, and discovery managers have ordered shutdown handlers.\\n\\n**Cleanup Ordering & Connection Draining:** The cleanup uses a structured shutdown pattern with `run.Group`:\\n1. **Termination Handler** (lines 1153-1177): Receives SIGTERM/SIGINT, signals `reloadReady` to stop accepting new work, and returns to trigger group shutdown\\n2. **Discovery Managers** (lines 1179-1205): Stopped first to prevent new target discovery\\n3. **Rule Manager** (lines 1207-1220): Stopped before scrape manager to avoid alerts during scraping shutdown\\n4. **Scrape Manager** (lines 1222-1244): Stopped after rule manager but before TSDB closure to prevent writes to closed storage\\n5. **Reload Handler** (lines 1261-1343): Waits for any in-progress reloads to complete before shutdown\\n6. **Configuration Loading** (lines 1346-1374): Waits for database to open\\n7. **TSDB** (lines 1376-1430+): Storage shutdown happens last\\n\\nEach component in the run.Group has a Run() function (execution) and an interrupt function. The web handler status is updated to `Stopping` state, notifications are added for shutdown, and the system gracefully waits for all goroutines to complete before exiting.\\n\\n### Key Patterns\\n\\n1. **Kubernetes** emphasizes lifecycle signal coordination with configurable delays and timeouts for different phases\\n2. **Grafana** uses simple timeout-based shutdown with context cancellation\\n3. **Prometheus** uses the run.Group pattern for dependency ordering and proper cleanup sequencing\\n\\nAll three implement proper SIGTERM/SIGINT handling, connection draining before shutdown, and timeout-bounded graceful termination to prevent indefinite hangs.\"\n}\n",
